SEMESTER S5 
PROCESS CONTROL INSTRUMENTATION 
 
Course Code 
PCICT502 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:1:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
4 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. Learn the basics of process control, including process variables, control actions, and 
process control block diagrams. 
2. Study control system objectives, evaluation criteria, and final control operations involving 
signal conversion, actuators, and control elements. 
3. Explore discontinuous and continuous controller modes, including proportional, integral, 
and derivative controls, as well as composite modes like PI, PD, and PID. 
4. Gain proficiency in multiple loop control systems, electronic and pneumatic controllers, 
process loop tuning methods, PLC programming, DCS architecture, and SCADA 
supervisory functions. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction to process control 
Process, process variables, need for process control, basic control actions, 
process control block diagram. 
Control system evaluation 
Control system objective, control  system evaluation criteria. 
Final control operation 
Signal conversion (analogue and digital electrical signals), actuators 
(electric, pneumatic and hydraulic), control elements (mechanical and 
electrical  valves). 
Controller principles 
 Process characteristics, control system  parameters. 
 
10  

 
 
2 
Discontinuous controller modes 
 Two position mode, multi- position mode, floating control mode. 
Continuous controller modes 
 Proportional controller mode, integral controller mode, derivative controller 
mode, composite controller modes-PI, PD and three mode. 
Control systems with multiple loops 
Feed forward control, practical aspects of the design of feed forward control, 
feed forward- feedback control, ratio control. 
 
11  
3 
Electronic controllers 
General features. Single mode and composite controller modes (P and PI 
controller design using OP AMP). 
Pneumatic controllers 
Continuous controller modes (Principle and Design of P, PI, PD, PID control 
modes). 
Process loop tuning 
Tuning of controllers, Cohen-Coon method of tuning (process reaction curve 
method). Ultimate cycle method (Ziegler Nichol’s method). Damped 
oscillation method. Frequency response method. Comparing tuning methods. 
12  
4 
Programmable logic controller (PLC) 
PLC versus relay, evolution of PLC, functions of PLC, advantages. PLC 
Programming -Basics of Ladder  Programming, on/off instructions, 
internal relay, jump instructions, data handling instruction, data 
manipulation instructions, Arithmetic and Comparison ,PID and other 
important instructions .Timers and Counters in PLC 
Distributed Control System (DCS) 
Introduction to DCS, evolution of DCS, DCS flow sheet symbols, 
architecture of DCS. 
SCADA  
Introduction to Supervisory computer tasks and DCS configuration: 
supervisory computer functions. 
 
11

Course Objectives: 
1. To provide a thorough understanding of the principles and techniques involved in flow 
measurement, including the various types of flow meters and their applications. 
2. To equip students with the knowledge of fluid mechanics, flow meter linearization and 
compensation, differential pressure flow meters, and control valve systems, enhancing their 
ability to apply this knowledge in practical scenarios.

SEMESTER S5 
ANALYTICAL INSTRUMENTATION 
 
Course Code 
PEICT521 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To understand the theory and operational principles of various instrumental methods 
    for qualitative and quantitative evaluation by different types of spectroscopy 
2. To review of important methods in the analysis of industrial gases and also to impart 
             fundamental knowledge on chromatography 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
UV-Vis, IR and fluorescence spectroscopy  
UV and Visible Spectroscopy: Colorimeters/ photometers: Single beam and 
double beam filter photometer – Spectro photometers: Single beam and 
double beam spectrophotometers. 
Infrared Spectrophotometers (NIR-Near IR): wave number, basic principle 
using diatomic harmonic structure, radiation sources, detectors. Fourier 
Transform Infrared Spectroscopy 
(FTIR). Raman spectroscopy: Raman Effect, basic principle, Raman 
spectrometer. 
Fluorescence spectroscopy: Principle of fluorescence – Measurement of 
fluorescence –Single beam and double beam filter fluorimeter- Ratio 
fluorimeter. Spectro fluorimeters. 
 
8  
2 
Photometry, Atomic Absorption spectrometer, and ESR Spectrometer  
Flame Photometry: Principle and constructional details of flame photometer- 
Emission system –Optical system – Detectors. 
Atomic Absorption spectrometer: basic block diagram, atomizers, 
nebulizers, plasma excitation sources, radiation sources 
12 

 
 
Electron Spin Resonance Spectrometers (ESR): Electron spin resonance, 
basic ESR spectrometer, microwave bridge, Klystrone, modulation, sample 
cavities. 
Mass, NMR spectroscopy and Gas Analysers 
Molecular Mass spectrometry: Principle of operation, Magnetic deflection 
mass spectrometers, Components of a mass spectrometer. 
Proton Nuclear Magnetic Resonance spectroscopy (NMR): Nuclear spin, 
resonance condition, relaxation condition 
Industrial Gas analysers- pH meters- Conductivity meters - Dissolved 
oxygen meters-Sodium analyser 
3 
Chromatography 
Chromatography: Chroma to graphic process–Classification- Terms in 
chromatography 
Gas chromatography: Block diagram, Principle, Constructional details, 
Column details, GC detector, katharometer, flame ionization detector, flame 
photometric detector, photo ionization detector, electro capture detector, 
argon ionization detector. 
  Liquid Chromatography: Types of liquid chromatography   (adsorption 
chromatography, partition chromatography, gel permeation chromatography, 
ion-exchange chromatography 
High pressure Liquid Chromatography (HPLC): Principle, Constructional 
details. 
 
8  
4 
UV-Vis, IR and fluorescence spectroscopy  
UV and Visible Spectroscopy: Colorimeters/ photometers: Single beam and 
double beam filter photometer – Spectro photometers: Single beam and 
double beam spectrophotometers. 
Infrared Spectrophotometers (NIR-Near IR): wave number, basic principle 
using diatomic harmonic structure, radiation sources, detectors. Fourier 
Transform Infrared Spectroscopy 
(FTIR). Raman spectroscopy: Raman Effect, basic principle, Raman 
spectrometer. 
Fluorescence spectroscopy: Principle of fluorescence – Measurement of 
fluorescence –Single beam and double beam filter fluorimeter- Ratio 
fluorimeter. Spectro fluorimeters. 
 
8

SEMESTER S5 
BIOMEDICAL INSTRUMENTATION 
 
Course Code 
PEICT522 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. 
Gain fundamental knowledge of biopotential acquisition and analysis:  
2. 
Develop an understanding of signal conditioning principles for biomedical   
applications 
3. 
Become familiar with the measurement of various physiological parameters  
                                                            SYLLABUS 
 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
BASIC ANATOMY AND PHYSIOLOGY: Origin of bio potential and its 
propagation, Nervous system, Muscular system, Cardiovascular system, 
Respiratory System. 
BIOPOTENTIAL 
ELECTRODES: 
Electrode-electrolyte 
interface, 
electrode–skin interface, half-cell potential, Contact impedance, polarization 
effects of electrode – non polarizable electrodes. Types of electrodes - 
surface, needle and micro electrodes and their equivalent circuits. Recording 
problems - motion artifacts- Monopolar and  bipolar electrode configurations  
 
9 
2 
Bio signals characteristics – frequency and amplitude ranges. ECG – 
Einthoven ‘s triangle, standard 12 lead system, Principles of vector 
cardiography. EEG – 10-20 electrode system, unipolar, bipolar and average 
mode. EMG– unipolar and bipolar mode. 
SIGNAL CONDITIONING CIRCUITS:  
Need for bio-amplifier - differential bio-amplifier, Design of bio-amplifiers 
 
9 

 
 
for the measurement of physiological variables. Power line interference, 
Band pass filtering. 
Working of isolation amplifiers, (transformer, capacitive and optical 
isolation), isolated DC amplifier and AC carrier amplifier. (Circuit diagram 
and working only) 
3 
MEASUREMENT OF NON-ELECTRICAL PARAMETERS: 
Temperature and pulse rate measurements. Blood Pressure: indirect methods 
- Auscultatory method, oscillometric method, direct methods: electronic 
manometer, Pressure amplifiers, Systolic, diastolic, mean detector circuit. 
Blood flow and cardiac output measurement: Indicator dilution, thermal 
dilution and dye dilution method, Electromagnetic and ultrasound blood flow 
measurement. 
Pulmonary 
function 
measurements-Spirometer, 
Photo 
plethysmography, Body plethysmography.  
7 
4 
ELECTRICAL SAFETY IN MEDICAL ENVIRONMENT: 
Types of Electrical hazards, Physiological effects of electric current –  
Threshold Values for Electrical Shock, shock hazards from electrical 
equipment – leakage current-Instruments for checking safety parameters of 
biomedical equipment, Methods of accident prevention, Electrical Safety 
Standards 
ASSISTIVE AND THERAPEUTIC EQUIPMENTS: 
Pacemakers, defibrillators, ventilators, diathermy, Heart-Lung machine and 
dialyzers. (Diagrams and Basic working only) 
BIOMEDICAL IMAGING  
X-ray, Computed Tomography, Ultrasound, Magnetic resonance Imaging. 
(Diagrams and Basic working only) 
 
11

SEMESTER S5 
POWER PLANT INSTRUMENTATION 
 
Course Code 
PEICT523 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
           PCICT402 
Course Type 
Theory Elective 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. 
Provide a comprehensive overview of various methods of power generation, including hydro, 
thermal, nuclear, solar, and wind power, with an emphasis on their processes, instrumentation, 
and control mechanisms. 
2. 
Equip students with knowledge about the critical role of instrumentation and control systems in 
power plant operations, including detailed study of boiler and turbine systems, and their 
measurement and control parameters. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Brief survey of methods of power generation-hydro, Thermal, Nuclear, Solar 
and Wind power, Power generation and distribution, Introduction to thermal 
power plant processes, Ideal steam cycles.  
Importance of instrumentation in power generation, Nuclear power plant 
instrumentation, Piping and instrumentation diagram of different types in 
nuclear power plant. Nuclear reactor control loops, Control and safety 
instrumentation, reliability aspects  
8 
 
 
2 
Boiler – types, Boiler - turbine units and its range systems, feed water 
systems, steam circuits, air preheating, air to fuel ratio.  
Soot blowers, combustion process, products of combustion, fuel systems, 
treatment of flue gases, steam turbine, alternator, feed water conditioning, 
turbine bypass valves, details of boiler processes combined cycle power 
plant, burner tilting, and bypass damper. 
        9 
 
3 
Measurement in boiler and turbine: Metal temperature 
measurement in boilers, Measurements of non-electrical parameters in power 
9 

 
 
plants – flow of feed water, fuel, air and steam with correction factor for 
temperature – steam pressure and steam temperature measurement,  smoke 
and dust monitor, flame monitoring. Smoke density measurement , Drum 
level measurement, radiation detector, Distributed control system in power 
plants, Interlocks in boiler operation, Cooling system. 
4 
Controls in boiler:  feed water control, soot blowing operation, steam 
temperature control, Coordinated control, Combustion control – Main 
pressure air/fuel ratio, furnace draft and excess air control. 
Drum level control- two element and three-element control. Main and reheat 
steam temperature control 
Boiler following mode operation, turbine following mode operation, 
selection between boiler and turbine following modes. 
Introduction to turbine supervising system, Automatic turbine runs up 
systems,  
 
10

SEMESTER S5 
NUMERICAL COMPUTATION USING PYTHON 
 
Course Code 
PEICT524 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0 :0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory (Elective) 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To develop students' skills in applying numerical methods to analyse and interpret 
engineering data and solve real-world problems. 
2. To provide students with a solid foundation in numerical methods for solving engineering 
problems using Python. 
3. To enable students to implement numerical techniques for nonlinear equations, interpolation, 
integration, differentiation, and ordinary differential equations. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Root Finding Methods (6 Hours) (Derivation or proof not required) 
Bisection method; Newton-Raphson method; Secant method; False 
Position Method; Fixed-point iteration; Convergence and error analysis of 
root-finding methods. 
Solving nonlinear equations using the above methods in Python (2 
Hours) 
8  
2 
Interpolation (9 Hours) (Derivation or proof not required) 
Finite difference interpolation: Newton's finite and backward difference 
interpolation methods. 
Polynomial Interpolation: Lagrange interpolation and Newton’s divided 
difference interpolation. 
Spline Interpolation: Cubic splines and B-splines. 
11  

 
 
Error analysis in interpolation. 
Implementing interpolation methods in Python (2 Hours) 
3 
Numerical Integration and Differentiation (6 Hours) 
Numerical Differentiation: Finite difference methods; Error analysis in 
numerical differentiation. 
Numerical Integration: Trapezoidal rule, Simpson’s rule, Gaussian 
quadrature, Adaptive quadrature methods. 
Writing Python programs to perform numerical differentiation and 
integration (2 Hours) 
8  
4 
Solution of Ordinary Differential Equations (7 Hours) 
Initial Value Problems: Euler’s method; Runge-Kutta methods; Multistep 
methods (Adams-Bashforth and Adams-Moulton methods). 
Boundary Value Problems: Shooting method; Finite difference method. 
Solving ODEs using Python (2 Hours) 
9

VLSI DESIGN 
 
Course Code 
PEICT526 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. This course aims to develop the skill to design various VLSI circuits 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Overview of CMOS device fundamentals . The CMOS inverter: - Voltage 
Transfer Characteristics, SPICE Description, Static Behavior - Switching 
Threshold - Noise Margins, Dynamic behavior - Device Capacitances - 
Propagation Delay - Power Consumption. 
 
9 
2 
CMOS fabrication Processes: -N-Tub, P-Tub and Twin Tub. MOS Circuit 
Layout - Stick diagrams, Layout design rules, Transistor layout - PMOS 
and NMOS, Gate Layout - Inverter, NAND, NOR and XOR, Layout 
generation using MICROWIND tool (For Assignments/Projects only). 
 
9  
3 
Combinational logic Circuits: - Static MOS - Complementary MOS - 
Ratioed logic - Pass Transistor logic - Differential Pass Transistor Logic - 
Transmission gate logic, Dynamic MOS - Basic Principles - Speed and 
power Dissipation - Signal Integrity issues. 
9  
4 
Sequential Logic Circuits: -Timing Metrics for sequential circuits, Static 
Latches and Registers, Dynamic Latches and Registers. Datapath 
Subsystems: - Adder - Ripple carry Adder - Full adder - Carry chain Adder 
- Carry-Bypass Adder - Carry Select Adder - Carry Look Ahead Adder, 
Multiplier - Array Multiplier - Carry Save Multiplier, Shifter - Barrel 
Shifter - Logarithmic Shifter. 
 
9

Continuous Assessment (25 Marks) 
1. Preparation and Pre-Lab Work (7 Marks) 
 
Pre-Lab Assignments: Assessment of pre-lab assignments or quizzes that test 
understanding of the upcoming experiment. 
 
Understanding of Theory: Evaluation based on students’ preparation and understanding 
of the theoretical background related to the experiments. 
 
2. Conduct of Experiments (7 Marks) 
 
Procedure and Execution: Adherence to correct procedures, accurate execution of 
experiments, and following safety protocols. 
 
Skill Proficiency: Proficiency in handling equipment, accuracy in observations, and 
troubleshooting skills during the experiments. 
 Teamwork: Collaboration and participation in group experiments. 
3. Lab Reports and Record Keeping (6 Marks) 
 
Quality of Reports: Clarity, completeness and accuracy of lab reports. Proper 
documentation of experiments, data analysis and conclusions. 
 
Timely Submission: Adhering to deadlines for submitting lab reports/rough record and 
maintaining a well-organized fair record. 
 
4. Viva Voce (5 Marks) 
 Oral Examination: Ability to explain the experiment, results and underlying 
principles during a viva voce session. 

 
 
Final Marks Averaging: The final marks for preparation, conduct of experiments, viva, 
and record are the average of all the specified experiments in the syllabus. 
Evaluation Pattern for End Semester Examination (50 Marks) 
1. Procedure/Preliminary Work/Design/Algorithm (10 Marks) 
 
Procedure Understanding and Description: Clarity in explaining the procedure and 
understanding each step involved. 
 
Preliminary Work and Planning: Thoroughness in planning and organizing 
materials/equipment. 
 
Algorithm Development: Correctness and efficiency of the algorithm related to the 
experiment. 
 
Creativity and logic in algorithm or experimental design. 
 
2. Conduct of Experiment/Execution of Work/Programming (15 Marks) 
 
Setup and Execution: Proper setup and accurate execution of the experiment or 
programming task. 
3. Result with Valid Inference/Quality of Output (10 Marks) 
 
Accuracy of Results: Precision and correctness of the obtained results. 
 
Analysis and Interpretation: Validity of inferences drawn from the experiment or 
quality of program output. 
 
4. Viva Voce (10 Marks) 
 
Ability to explain the experiment, procedure results and answer related questions 
 
Proficiency in answering questions related to theoretical and practical aspects of the 
subject. 
 
5. Record (5 Marks) 
 Completeness, clarity, and accuracy of the lab record submitted

 
 
SEMESTER: S5 
  INDUSTRIAL INSTRUMENTATION & IOT LAB  
 
Course Code 
PCICL508 
CIE Marks 
50 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
0:0:3:0 
ESE Marks  
50 
Credits 
2 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
PCICT503,PCICT
402 
Course Type 
Lab 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. Enable students to gain hands-on experience in measuring temperature, viscosity, pressure, 
level, and speed using various instruments like Optical Pyrometer, viscometers, bourdon 
pressure gauge, Capacitive transducer, and Cup anemometer. 
2. Equip students with the ability to design and implement temperature measurement 
instruments and interface them with computers. 
3. Provide students with insights into the characteristics of control valves, transmitters (level, 
flow, temperature, pressure), and the dynamic response of second-order systems 
Expt.  
No. 
Experiments 
A) Measurement experiments (4 out of 6 experiment is mandatory) 
1 
Measurement of temperature using Optical Pyrometer.
2 
Measurement of Viscosity using red wood viscometer.
3 
Measurement of Viscosity using rotational viscometer.
4 
Calibration of bourdon pressure gauge using Dead weight pressure gauge tester.
5 
Measurement of (1) level using Capacitive transducer (2) speed using Cup anemometer.
6 
Study the principle of operation of a gyroscope and sonic range finder
B) Design of Industrial instruments (3 out of 5 experiment is mandatory)
7 
Design a thermometer using platinum RTD as sensor with the following specification. 
Temp range: - -2000c to +2000c 
Output Voltage: - -2Volt to 2Volt 
Also interface the thermometer with computer using any data acquisition system 
(preferably NI DAQ and LabView software) (mandatory experiment) 
8 
Design a thermometer using NTC thermistor as the sensor with the following 
specification

SEMESTER S6 
DISCRETE TIME SIGNAL PROCESSING 
Course Code 
PCICT601 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:1:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
4 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
PCICT403 Signals 
and Systems 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. Equip students with the foundational knowledge of discrete time signal processing techniques 
and digital filtering. 
2. Enable students to apply digital signal processing techniques in their engineering careers 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
DISCRETE FOURIER TRANSFORM 
Review of Discrete Time Fourier Transform. 
Frequency domain sampling and reconstruction of Discrete time signals -
DFT- properties of DFT. Circular convolution - Dentition, Linear 
convolution using DFT.  
Computation of DFT - Direct computation of DFT – DFT as linear 
Transformation – Fast Fourier Transform (Radix – 2 FFT only) – 
Decimation in time and decimation in frequency algorithms. 
Problem solving using software tools. 
 
11 
2 
DIGITAL FILTER STRUCTURES 
Z-Transform representation of FIR and IIR filters- FIR filter structures: - 
Direct form, Cascade form and Lattice structures  
IIR filter structure: Direct form Transpose form, Cascade form and Parallel 
form structures. 
FINITE WORD LENGTH EFFECTS 
Quantization noise, Round off effects, Limit cycle oscillations. 
 
11 

 
 
3 
IIR DIGITAL FILTERS  
Digital Filter Specifications – Design of IIR digital filters from analog filters 
– Butterworth and Chebyshev filters – Design of Low pass filters – Spectral 
transformation of IIR filters –Analogue to digital transfer function: impulse 
invariant method, bilinear transformation method. 
Problem solving using software tools. 
11 
4 
FIR DIGITAL FILTERS 
Design of FIR filters: Estimation of filter order - FIR filter design - Impulse 
response of ideal filters - Gibbs Phenomenon – Fixed window functions: 
Rectangular, Hamming, Blackman –Adjustable window function: Kaiser 
window. 
Problem solving using software tools. 
 
11

SEMESTER S6 
INSTRUMENTATION SYSTEM DESIGN 
Course Code 
PCICT602 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
(PCICT502 & 
PCICT503)
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. Improve the ability of students to comprehend and design various types of instrumentation 
systems. 
 
2. To get a thorough knowledge about electric and intrinsic aspect of safety while designing an 
instrumentation system 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction to Instrumentation system design- System configuration- 
Problem analysis Experimental engineering analysis- Instrument design- 
The designer’s viewpoint. 
Electronic processing modules for handling transducer output- P/I 
Conversion- I/P conversion- V/I and I/V - conversion -Carrier amplifier, 
Charge amplifier- Impedance converters - Phase sensitive detector -RMS 
converters- Ratio metric conversion- Logarithmic compression 
Design of thermo couple circuitry with cold junction compensation, 
linearization, amplification and conversion of its output to 4 to 20 ma 
current. Design of RTD with lead wire compensation and conversion of its 
output to 4 to 20 ma current. Design of Capacitance based Level 
Transmitter for both conducting and non-conducting liquids - Signal 
conditioning circuit for pH measurement. 
 
12 
2 
Piping and instrumentation diagram. Introduction to process piping- 
Material selection- Pipe fitting. Cabling- General requirements- Cable 
types- Cable segregation Earthing – pre installation testing- piping and 
cable testing- loop testing 
 
8 

 
 
Instrument project control- Documents to be produced- Process flow- 
Mechanical flow. Instrument index and instrument specification sheets- 
Loop wiring diagrams-Panel drawing and specification- Instrument 
specification and standard- Piping specifications- Electrical specification- 
Bid documents- Project procedures- Project scheduler work- Co-
ordination. Project manager- Process engineers- Equipment engineers –
Piping design supervisor- Job execution- Planning hints- scheduling- 
Specifying instruments-  
3 
Specification of various measurement and control loops (flow, pressure, 
level, temperature etc.)  
Processes connections- Location of taps- sealing Instruments from process- 
Manifolds and gauge valves- Selection of units- Charts and ranges- 
Instrument identification- Winderising Packaged equipment system. 
Construction - organizing- Documents required- Planning schedule- Cost 
control- Ordering and receiving equipment and method- Purchase order- 
Material status- Instrument installation and commissioning -Instrument 
piping and tubing system- Air supplies- Pneumatic signal - Checklist of 
installation practices - calibration- testing- typical flow transmitter checkout 
procedures – typical control valve-check out procedure. 
Plant commission - Testing and pre commissioning 
8 
4 
Control panels – Introduction- Control room lay out – Instrument power 
requirements and distribution Control room lighting- Communication 
system- Control panel types. Auxiliary racks and cabinet- Panel piping and 
tubing – Air headers- Graphic displays- Panel bid Specification. 
 Safety- Introduction- Electric circuits risk- Flammable atmosphere- Other 
safety aspects such as electrocution, let go current. Electrical Safety- 
Purging and pressurizing endorser- Safety precautions and parameters for 
industrial jobs- Intrinsic safety- Process safety and Safety Instrumented 
systems , Intrinsic safety barrier installation with suitable examples.  
 
8

SEMESTER S6 
REFINARY INSTRUMENTATION 
Course Code 
PEICT631 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To give an exposure on the important parameters to be monitored and analysed in a refinery 
and impart knowledge about various techniques used for the measurement and control in the 
refineries 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Origin of petroleum 
Oil and gas traps. Physical and chemical characteristics of crude oil, source 
rock and maturation. Migration of oil mechanism pattern and barriers, 
Reservoir rocks and cap rocks, Entrapment of oil-types and mechanism. 
Application of remote sensing in petroleum resource Development , Basin 
and exploration strategies. The model approach to exploration strategy, 
Basin mapping methods, Depositional systems such as marine, non-marine, 
coastal, shelf, carbonate evaporates, Basin evolution, Sedimentation and 
Plate tectonics. 
 
6  
2 
Important unit operations 
Drying-Separation-Heat Transfer-Distillation-Thermal cracking catalytic 
cracking catalytic reforming- hydro cracking – hydro treating. Chemical 
oxidation-Chemical reduction- Polymerisation. Alkylation-Isomerisation. 
 
10 
3 
Production of important petrochemicals 
Chemicals from petroleum -Methane derivatives- Acetylene derivatives- 
9 

 
 
Ethylene derivatives. Propylene derivatives - Cyclic petrochemicals. 
Production of Ethylene, Acetylene- and propylene from petroleum. 
4 
Controlling methods 
Process control in refinery and petrochemical industry-Control of distillation 
column, catalytic cracking unit, catalytic reformer, pyrolysis unit. Optimal 
control of cracking units. 
 
 
11

SEMESTER S6 
                       MICRO ELECTRO MECHANICAL SYSTEMS 
Course Code 
PEICT632 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
NIL 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To develop knowledge on Micro electro mechanical systems and materials used in the 
manufacture 
 
2. To understand various micro fabrication procedures, techniques and packaging considerations 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction to Micro Electronic Mechanical Systems: Materials for 
MEMS- silicon- structure and orientations, properties. Other materials- shape 
memory alloy (SMA), polymers, silicon compounds etc, material properties.  
Commercial MEMS structures and systems: 
Overview of commonly used mechanical structures in MEMS - Beams, 
Cantilevers, Plates, Diaphragms – Typical applications. Passive MEMS 
structures- fluid nozzles- ink jet nozzles. Sensors- piezoresistive pressure 
sensors- mass flow sensors- acceleration sensors, actuators- micro 
mechanical valves-micro pumps. 
 
9 
2 
Process of micromachining: Process of micromachining- pattern transfer 
using additive technique. Silicon growth- oxidation of silicon-molecular 
beam epitaxy. 
Physical vapour deposition (PVD)- sputtering- laser deposition- ion plating- 
cluster beam technology- Chemical vapour deposition (CVD)- step 
coverage- plasma enhanced CVD, Electron cyclotron resonance CVD 
(ECRCVD)- sol-gel deposition technique. 
 
9 
3 
Lithography 
9 

 
 
Photolithography- Introduction- masks- spinning- resist and soft backing- 
exposure and post exposure treatment- development- descumming and post 
baking- resists- wafer priming, wafer cleaning and contamination- clean 
room- resist striping. Next generation lithography-extreme ultra violet 
lithography (EUVL)- x-ray lithography- LIGA- charged particle beam 
lithography- electron beam lithography- ion beam lithography. 
Etching: Introduction- dry etching- physical etching- ion etching or 
sputtering- ion beam etching, plasma etching- deep reactive ion etching 
(DRIE)- isotropic wet etching- anisotropic wet etching. 
4 
MEMS packaging: Key design and packaging consideration- wafer stack 
thickness- wafer dicing concerns, thermal management- stress isolation- 
protective coating and media isolation. Wafer level packaging and die level 
packaging. Hermetic packaging- calibration and compensation- die attach 
process- solder alloy- bonding process using solder alloy- organic adhesive 
wiring and inter connections- Wire bonding- flip chip bonding- micro 
fluidics interconnections. 
Packaging material properties- mechanical- moisture penetration- interfacial 
adhesion, thermal- chemical- electrical. 
 
9

SEMESTER S6 
BIOMEDICAL SIGNAL PROCESSING 
Course Code 
PEICT633 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
PEICT 522 
Biomedical 
Instrumentation
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. Understand the fundamental concepts and characteristics of biomedical signals. 
2. Understand signal acquisition systems and advanced signal processing techniques. 
3. Apply signal processing knowledge to practical biomedical engineering challenges, 
including cardiological and neurological signal processing. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction to Biomedical Signals 
Introduction to Biomedical Signals, Characteristics of Biomedical Signals, 
Time-domain vs. frequency-domain representation 
Acquisition of Biomedical Signals 
Signal Acquisition Systems,  acquisition of biomedical signals like ECG, 
EEG and EMG , Analog-to-digital conversion (ADC),  
Nyquist theorem and its importance in signal acquisition, Aliasing,  Signal 
conversion circuits 
 
9 
2 
The Fourier transform, Correlation, Convolution, Power spectrum estimation 
Adaptive filters: Principle of noise canceller model, 60 Hz adaptive 
cancelling using a sine wave model 
Adaptive and optimal filtering ‐ Modelling of Biomedical signals ‐ Detection 
of biomedical signals in noise ‐ removal of artifacts of one signal embedded 
in another ‐ Maternal‐Fetal ECG  
Signal Averaging: Basics of signal averaging, signal averaging as a digital 
filter, a typical averager. 
9 

 
 
Turning point algorithm, AZTEC algorithm, CORTES algorithm, Fan 
algorithm, Huffman coding 
3 
Cardiological Signal Processing 
Basics of ECG, Anatomy of the heart and electrical activity 
Basics of ECG waveform and lead systems,  Methods and devices for ECG 
signal acquisition, Noise & artifacts, Preprocessing of ECG Signals Noise 
removal and baseline correction, Feature Extraction-detection of P, QRS, and 
T waves, Heart rate variability analysis 
Advanced ECG Processing 
 Arrhythmia 
Detection- 
Algorithms 
for 
arrhythmia 
detection 
and 
classification 
9 
4 
Neurological signal processing  
 Basics of EEG and its characteristics, Brain anatomy and electrical 
activity, basics of EEG waveform and electrode placement, methods and 
devices for EEG signal acquisition, detection of EEG rhythms, template 
matching for EEG spike and wave detection 
Preprocessing of EEG Signals- Noise removal and artifact reduction 
Feature Extraction- Time-frequency analysis, power spectral density 
 Advanced EEG Processing 
 Brain-Computer Interface (BCI), Introduction to BCI and its applications 
9

SEMESTER S6 
COMMUNICATION SYSTEM AND TELEMETRY 
Course Code 
PEICT634 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R)

Credits

2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any)

Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To understand and analyse the principles of communication and telemetry. 
 
2. Telemetry automatically collects, transmits and measures data from remote sources, using 
sensors and other devices to collect data. It uses communication systems to transmit the data 
back to a central location. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours

of AM and FM.

amplitude modulation- Pulse time modulation- Pulse width modulation 
Principles of Pulse Code Modulation-Delta Modulation-PSK, ASK, FSK

2

telemetry-Optical telemetry. Transducers for Telemetry Methods of

SEMESTER S6 
TOTAL QUALITY MANAGEMENT 
Course Code 
PEICT636 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. Study the concepts of total quality management, employee involvement and quality planning. 
2. Study the importance of quality of service ,role of reliability and statistical tools for 
measuring quality. 
3. Identify the importance of continuous process improvement in quality, suppliers, 
benchmarking and quality function deployment. 
4. Identify the importance of total productive maintenance, failure mode and effect analysis, 
need for ISO systems and quality auditing.

SEMESTER 6 
PLC AND DCS 
Course Code 
PEICT635 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
5/3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hr.30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. Learn the roles, architectures, and interfacing techniques of computer-based measurement and 
control systems, including HMI and hardware integration. 
2. Gain hands-on experience with PLC programming and simulation, and understand the 
functionalities and interfacing of Distributed Control Systems for process control. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction to computer based control system -Role of computers in 
measurement and (process) control   Basic components of computer based 
measurement and control systems Architecture – computer based process 
control system –Centralised, Distributed and Hierarchical.  Human Machine 
Interface (HMI) Hardware for computer based process control system, 
Interfacing computer system with process. 
Architecture of DDC, SCADA and DCS. 
Programmable logic Controller (PLC): Introduction, Evolution, Relay VS 
PLC VS Computer 
9 
2 
PLC- Hardware and Internal Architecture-Input –output devices .Basics of 
Ladder  Programming, on/off instructions, internal relay, jump instructions, 
data handling instruction, data manipulation instructions, Arithmetic and 
Comparison ,PID and other important instructions  
9 
3 
Timers and Counters in PLC. Problems. Design Development and 
Simulation of PLC Programme Program on Temperature control Valve 
sequencing, Conveyor belt control and Control of a process. 
9 

 
 
PLC Installation, trouble shooting and maintenance, Design of Alarms and 
Interlocks, Networks of PLC 
Distributed Control System- DCS - Evolution– Various Architectures – 
Comparison – Local control unit  
4 
DCS -LCU Languages-Process interfacing issues-communication facilities-
Operator interface-Low level and High level Operator interface- Displays - 
Engineering interfaces – Low level and high level engineering interfaces – 
Factors to be considered in selecting DCS – Other key issues in DCS –
Packaging and Power system issues. 
9

SEMESTER S6 
MODERN CONTROL ENGINEERING 
Course Code 
PBICT604 
CIE Marks 
60 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:1 
ESE Marks 
40 
Credits 
4 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
PCICT501 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To equip students with advanced techniques in designing cascade compensators using root-
locus and Bode plot methods. 
2. To enable students to model and analyse continuous linear time-invariant (LTI) systems using 
state-space representations 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Design of Cascade Compensators (10 Hours) 
Dominant pole; realisation of basic compensators: lead, lag, lag, and lag-
lead compensator. 
Cascade compensation using root-locus: lead, lag, and lead-lag 
compensation. 
Cascade compensation using bode plot: lag, lead, and lag-lead compensation. 
 
10 
2 
State Space Modelling of Continuous Linear Time-Invariant Systems 
(9 Hours) 
Concept of state, state variable, state vector and state space; State models 
for linear continuous-time systems; State variable representation of 
continuous-time systems using physical variables. 
Transfer function from state variable model; transformation of state 
variables and invariance property. 
State space representation using phase variable (state space 
representation from transfer function): Controllable canonical form, 
observable canonical form, Jordan Canonical Form. 
 
9 

 
 
3 
State Variable Analysis of Continuous LTI Systems (8 Hours) 
Solution of state equation; state transition matrix; properties of state 
transition matrix. 
Computation of the state transition matrix using Lyapunov’s 
Method and Cayley Hamilton theorem; Response of homogeneous and 
non-homogeneous state-space model. 
Concept of controllability and observability; Kalaman test. 
8 
4 
State Variable Design (Continuous) (6 Hours) 
Design of state variable feedback if the given model is in the controllable 
canonical form; design of arbitrary state variable feedback if the given 
model is not in controllable canonical form. 
Design of full order state observer; application of duality Principle; 
concept of reduced order state-observer. 
Stability analysis of Continuous LTI Systems using Phase Plane 
Method (3 Hours) 
Singular points, classification of singular points. 
 
9 
Suggestion on Project Topics

Course Outcomes (COs) 
At the end of the course students should be able to:  
Course Outcome 
Bloom’s 
Knowledge 
Level (KL) 
CO1 
Apply the concepts of dominant pole placement to design and 
implement lead, lag, and lead-lag compensators using root-locus and 
Bode plot techniques. 
K3 
CO2 
Construct state-space models for continuous-time LTI systems and 
derive transfer functions from state variable representations. 
K3 
CO3 
Compute and utilise the state transition matrix to analyse the response 
of continuous-time LTI systems. 
K4 
CO4 
Design and implement state variable feedback controllers and state 
observers for continuous-time LTI systems to achieve desired system 
performance. 
K3 
CO5 
Evaluate the stability and performance of a continuous LTI system 
using phase plane methods and design compensators or state feedback 
mechanisms to enhance system stability and performance based on 
project requirements. 
K5

SEMESTER S6 
DESIGN THINKING AND PRODUCT DEVELOPMENT 
(Common to Group A & Group B) 
Course Code 
GXEST605 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
2:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
2 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None
 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To guide students through the iterative stages of design thinking, including empathizing with 
users, defining problems, ideating solutions and developing Proof of Concepts (PoC) and 
technical feasibility studies. 
2. To promote the development of critical thinking skills by engaging students in integrative 
inquiry, where they ask meaningful questions that connect classroom knowledge with real-
world applications. 
3. To equip students with the ability to involve in product design considering the sustainability, 
inclusivity, diversity and equity aspects. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Fundamentals of design thinking and product development: Overview of 
stages of product development lifecycle; Design thinking -Definition-Design 
thinking for product innovation; Bringing social impact in ideation-
Identifying societal needs-understanding multi-faceted issues-community 
engagement and empathetic design- technological innovation meeting 
societal needs; Understanding and Bridging the divide using Human 
Centered Design (HCD); Designing for inclusivity in product development-
embracing user diversity - Long term impact - sustainability encompassing 
environmental,economic and social dimensions; Technology Readiness 
Level in the Innovation Life-cycle; Performing a self-check on innovative 
6 

 
 
ideas - Originality of idea- understanding innovation landscape - 
patentability - understanding the economic landscape - Unique Selling 
Proposition (USP) - Repeatability and Manufacturability - Sustainability - 
Leveraging business models for comprehensive analysis 
2 
Empathize: Design thinking phases; Role of empathy in design thinking; 
Methods of empathize phase - Ask 5 Why/ 5 W+H questions;  Empathy 
maps -  Things to be done prior to empathy mapping - Activities during and 
after the session; Understanding empathy tools - Customer Journey Map - 
Personas. 
Define: Methods of Define Phase: Storytelling, Critical items diagrams, 
Define success. 
6 
3 
Ideation : Stages of ideation; Techniques and tools - Divergent thinking 
tools - Convergent thinking tools - Idea capturing tools; Cross-industry 
inspiration; Role of research in ideation - Market research - consumer 
research - leveraging research for informed ideation; Technological trends - 
navigating the technological landscape - Integrating emerging technologies; 
Feasibility studies - technical, economic, market, operational, legal,  and 
ethical feasibility; Ideation session- techniques and tips. 
Proof of Concept (PoC) : Setting objectives; Risk assessment; Technology 
scouting; Document and process management; Change management; 
Knowledge Capture; Validating PoC; Story telling in PoC presentation 
6 
4 
Design: Navigating from PoC to detailed design; Developing Specification 
Requirement Document (SRD)/Software Requirement Specification (SRS); 
Design for manufacturability; Industrial standards and readability of code; 
Design to cost; Pre-compliance; Optimized code; Design Failure Mode and 
Effects Analysis (DFMEA); Forecasting future design changes. 
Prototyping: Alpha prototypes; Beta prototypes; Transition from design to 
prototype; Goals and expectations for Alpha and Beta prototypes; Effective 
strategies for maintaining timeline in prototyping; Testing and refining 
Alpha prototypes; Transitioning to Beta prototypes. 
Pilot build: Definition and purpose of a pilot build; setting objectives; 
Identification and selection of manufacturing partner for pilot build; Testing 
procedures in pilot build; Scaling from pilot build to full-scale production / 
implementation. 
6

Sample Assignments: 
1. Evaluate and prepare a report on how the aspects including inclusivity, diversity and equity are taken 
into consideration during the empathize and define phases of the Miniproject course. 
2. Evaluate and prepare a report on how the aspects including sustainability, inclusivity, diversity and 
equity are taken into consideration during the ideate phase of the Miniproject course. 
3. Evaluate and prepare a report on how User-Centric Design (UCD) is used in the design and 
development of PoC of the product being developed in the Miniproject course. 
4. Prepare a plan for the prototype building of the product being developed in the Miniproject course. 
5. Report on the activities during the empathize phase including the maps & other materials created 
during the sessions. 
6. Report on the activities during the define phase including the maps & other materials created during 
the sessions. 
7. Report of all the ideas created during the ideation phase of the Miniproject course through the tools 
including SCAMPER technique, SWOT analysis, Decision matrix analysis, six thinking hats 
exercise 
8. Prepare a full scale production plan for the product being developed in the Miniproject course. 
9. Create a Stanford Business Model Canvas related to the Miniproject. 
An industrial visit of at least a day for experiential learning and submit a report on the learnings, for 
example industry standards and procedures.

SEMESTER S6 
BASICS OF INSTRUMENTATION ENGINEERING 
Course Code 
OEICT 611 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. Understand the Fundamentals of Instrumentation and Control Engineering and functional 
elements of measurement systems. 
2. Describe about functions of a control system and master Instrument Characteristics. 
3. Study input-output configuration of instruments and develop Proficiency in Calibration  
4. Analyse and Mitigate Measurement Errors and measurement noise. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
INTRODUCTION 
TO 
INSTRUMENTATION 
& 
CONTROL 
ENGINEERING- Definition-scope and importance- application of 
instrumentation in different fields like petrochemical, Biomedical, 
pharmaceutical and food processing. 
FUNCTIONAL ELEMENTS OF MEASUREMENT SYSTEM 
Introduction to instrument systems - Typical applications of instrument 
systems. Basic description of the functional elements of the measurement 
system with examples. 
TRANSDUCERS AND INSTRUMENT TYPES 
Definition of transducers. Role of transducers in instrumentation. 
Classification of instruments: Active and passive instruments - Null-type and 
deflection-type instruments - Analogue and digital instruments - Indicating 
instruments and instruments with a signal output -Manually operated and 
automatic type, Self-generating and power operated types, Contacting and 
 
9 

 
 
non-contacting types - Smart and non-smart instruments.              
2 
FUNCTIONAL ELEMENTS OF CONTROL SYSTEM 
Need of Control systems – Role of error detectors – Block diagram for a 
control system with examples.  
MEASUREMENT SYSTEM PERFORMANCE  
Static characteristics of instruments. 
Accuracy and precision, static sensitivity, linearity, hysteresis, threshold, 
dead time, dead zone, resolution or discrimination. static error, static 
correction. Scale range and span, reproducibility and drift, repeatability.  
Dynamic characteristics of instruments.  
Understating of (1) Zero order instrument (2) First order instrument (3) 
Second order instrument. 
 
9 
3 
CALIBRATION OF MEASURING SENSORS AND INSTRUMENTS  
Standards and calibration - Necessity of calibration- Careful instrument 
design, Principles of calibration - Control of calibration environment - 
Calibration chain and traceability - Calibration records  - 
Intelligent 
instruments. 
TYPES OF INPUTS 
Input output configuration of measuring instruments and measurement 
systems. Desired inputs, interfering inputs, modifying inputs. Methods of 
correction for interfering and modifying inputs. 
Loading effects. Input and output impedances. Input impedances, input 
admittance, output impedances, output admittance. 
9 
4 
MEASUREMENT NOISE  
Noise, signal to noise ratio, sources of noise, Johnson noise, power spectrum 
density. Sources of measurement noise - Inductive coupling - Capacitive 
(electrostatic) coupling - Noise due to multiple earths - Noise in the form 
of voltage.  
ERRORS DURING THE MEASUREMENT PROCESS 
Errors in measurements, true value, Limiting errors (Guarantee errors). 
 
9 

 
 
Relative (fractional) limiting error. Combination of quantities with limiting 
errors. Known errors, types of errors, gross errors, systematic errors, 
instrumental errors, environmental errors, observational errors. Random 
(residual) errors.  
Reduction of systematic errors - Careful instrument design - 
Method of opposing inputs - Calibration - Manual correction of 
output reading.

SEMESTER S6 
 MICRO ELECTRO MECHANICAL SYSTEMS 
Course Code 
OEICT612 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
NIL 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To develop knowledge on Micro electro mechanical systems and materials used in the 
manufacture 
2. To understand various micro fabrication procedures, techniques and packaging considerations 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction to Micro Electronic Mechanical Systems: Materials for 
MEMS- silicon- structure and orientations, properties. Other materials- shape 
memory alloy (SMA), polymers, silicon compounds etc, material properties.  
Commercial MEMS structures and systems: 
Overview of commonly used mechanical structures in MEMS - Beams, 
Cantilevers, Plates, Diaphragms – Typical applications. Passive MEMS 
structures- fluid nozzles- ink jet nozzles. Sensors- piezoresistive pressure 
sensors- mass flow sensors- acceleration sensors, actuators- micro 
mechanical valves-micro pumps. 
 
9 
2 
Process of micromachining: Process of micromachining- pattern transfer 
using additive technique. Silicon 
growth- oxidation of silicon-molecular beam epitaxy. 
Physical vapour deposition (PVD)- sputtering- laser deposition- ion plating- 
cluster beam technology- Chemical vapour deposition (CVD)- step 
 
9 

 
 
coverage- plasma enhanced CVD, Electron cyclotron resonance CVD 
(ECRCVD)- sol-gel deposition technique. 
3 
Lithography 
Photolithography- Introduction- masks- spinning- resist and soft backing- 
exposure and post exposure treatment- development- descumming and post 
baking- resists- wafer priming, wafer cleaning and contamination- clean 
room- resist striping. Next generation lithography-extreme ultra violet 
lithography (EUVL)- x-ray lithography- LIGA- charged particle beam 
lithography- electron beam lithography- ion beam lithography. 
Etching: Introduction- dry etching- physical etching- ion etching or 
sputtering- ion beam etching, plasma etching- deep reactive ion etching 
(DRIE)- isotropic wet etching- anisotropic wet etching. 
9 
4 
MEMS packaging: Key design and packaging consideration- wafer stack 
thickness- wafer dicing concerns, thermal management- stress isolation- 
protective coating and media isolation. Wafer level packaging and die level 
packaging. Hermetic packaging- calibration and compensation- die attach 
process- solder alloy- bonding process using solder alloy- organic adhesive 
wiring and inter connections- Wire bonding- flip chip bonding- micro 
fluidics interconnections. 
Packaging material properties- mechanical- moisture penetration- interfacial 
adhesion, thermal- chemical- electrical. 
 
9

SEMESTER S6 
INSTRUMENTATION FOR AGRICULTUTRE 
Course Code 
OEICT 613 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To expose the students about various instruments used in agriculture 
2. To teach the design of greenhouses using various instruments 
3. To impart ideas about modern technologies used in agriculture  
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
  Soil Science & Sensors
Soil science :  fundamental definitions & relationships 
properties of soil :  index properties of soil,  Engineering properties 
of soil,  physical properties of soil 
permeability & seepage analysis,  Mohr’s circle of stress 
Necessity of instrumentation & control for agriculture 
Sensors and transducers: definitions,  introduction to sonic 
anemometers,  hygrometers,  thermocouples,  close path gas 
analysers,  introduction to various biosensors 
 
9 
2 
 Instrumentation in industrial Continuous & Batch processes 
Idea about continuous and batch processes 
Flow diagram of sugar plant, sensors & instrumentation set up 
Flow diagram of fermenter, sensors & instrumentation set up 
Flow diagram of dairy industry & instrumentation set up for it 
 
9 

 
 
Juice extraction control process & instrumentation set up.  
Oil extraction plant and instrumentation set up for it. 
Pesticides manufacturing process and control 
3 
  Instrumentation in Irrigation 
Necessity of irrigation in agriculture 
Evapotranspiration and its measurement methods 
irrigation methods: overhead, centre pivot, lateral move, micro 
irrigation systems & the comparison of different irrigation systems 
soil moisture measurement methods: resistance-based method, 
voltage based method, thermal based method 
Water distribution & management control, Auto drip & sprinkler 
irrigation systems,  
Irrigation canal management systems 
upstream & downstream control concept 
Introduction to SCADA , Applications of SCADA in agriculture 
11 
4 
Greenhouse Parameters & Instrumentation 
Greenhouse effect, Concept & construction of green houses, 
ventilation, cooling & heating, wind speed, temperature & 
humidity, soil moisture, rain gauge, carbon dioxide enrichment 
measurement & control 
implementation of hydraulic, pneumatic & electronics control 
circuits in harvesters cotton pickers, tractor 
Classification of pumps: pump characteristics, pump selection & 
installation. 
 
9

SEMESTER: S6 
PROCESS CONTROL INSTRUMENTATION LAB 
Course Code 
PCICL607 
CIE Marks 
50 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
0:0:3:0 
50 
Credits 
2 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
PROCESS CONTROL 
INSTRUMENTATION 
Course Type 
Lab 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. Develop a comprehensive understanding of various control modes and their applications 
through hands-on experiments 
2. Acquire practical skills in advanced process control and automation technologies 
Expt.  
No. 
Experiments 
 
Part A 
Process Control Modes (All experiments are mandatory. Students must 
compare the performance of different process stations and the effect of 
adding different process control modes.) 
1 
Familiarisation of ON-OFF, proportional, proportional plus integral, and proportional 
plus integral plus derivative control mode using pressure process station or flow 
process station and Construction of ISA diagram.  
2 
Familiarisation of ON-OFF, proportional, proportional plus integral, and proportional 
plus integral plus derivative control mode using level process station or temperature 
process station and Construction of ISA diagram.  
3 
Tuning of P, PI, and PID control mode for any one process station using Ziegler 
Nichols open-loop method.  
4

5

Continuous Assessment (25 Marks) 
1. Preparation and Pre-Lab Work (7 Marks) 
 
Pre-Lab Assignments: Assessment of pre-lab assignments or quizzes that test 
understanding of the upcoming experiment. 
 
Understanding of Theory: Evaluation based on students’ preparation and understanding 
of the theoretical background related to the experiments. 
2. Conduct of Experiments (7 Marks) 
 
Procedure and Execution: Adherence to correct procedures, accurate execution of 
experiments, and following safety protocols. 
 
Skill Proficiency: Proficiency in handling equipment, accuracy in observations, and 
troubleshooting skills during the experiments. 
 Teamwork: Collaboration and participation in group experiments. 
3. Lab Reports and Record Keeping (6 Marks) 
 
Quality of Reports: Clarity, completeness and accuracy of lab reports. Proper 
documentation of experiments, data analysis and conclusions. 
 
Timely Submission: Adhering to deadlines for submitting lab reports/rough record and 
maintaining a well-organized fair record. 
 
4. Viva Voce (5 Marks) 
 Oral Examination: Ability to explain the experiment, results and underlying 
principles during a viva voce session. 
Final Marks Averaging: The final marks for preparation, conduct of experiments, viva, 
and record are the average of all the specified experiments in the syllabus. 
Evaluation Pattern for End Semester Examination (50 Marks) 
1. Procedure/Preliminary Work/Design/Algorithm (10 Marks) 
 
Procedure Understanding and Description: Clarity in explaining the procedure and 
understanding each step involved. 
 
Preliminary Work and Planning: Thoroughness in planning and organizing 
materials/equipment. 

 
 
 
Algorithm Development: Correctness and efficiency of the algorithm related to the 
experiment. 
 
Creativity and logic in algorithm or experimental design. 
 
2. Conduct of Experiment/Execution of Work/Programming (15 Marks) 
 
Setup and Execution: Proper setup and accurate execution of the experiment or 
programming task. 
3. Result with Valid Inference/Quality of Output (10 Marks) 
 
Accuracy of Results: Precision and correctness of the obtained results. 
 
Analysis and Interpretation: Validity of inferences drawn from the experiment or 
quality of program output. 
 
4. Viva Voce (10 Marks) 
 
Ability to explain the experiment, procedure results and answer related questions 
 
Proficiency in answering questions related to theoretical and practical aspects of the 
subject. 
 
5. Record (5 Marks) 
 Completeness, clarity, and accuracy of the lab record submitted

SEMESTER S7 
DIGITAL CONTROL 
Course Code 
PEICT741 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
PBICT604 
Course Type 
Theory 
Course Objectives: 
1. Introduce fundamental concepts of digital control systems, including discrete-time system 
representation, sampling processes, and the effects of sampling periods on system 
behavior. 
2.  Provide methods for modeling discrete-time systems, focusing on Z-transforms, s-plane 
to z-plane mapping, and stability analysis techniques such as Jury stability test and bi-
linear transformation. 
3. Develop skills for designing digital control systems using frequency response plots, root 
locus plots, and z-plane synthesis, addressing both transient and steady-state responses. 
4. Explore discrete state-space models, including state variable representations, stability 
analysis via Lyapunov's theorem, and advanced design techniques such as pole 
placement, observer design, and state feedback design. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction to digital control-Discrete time system representation- Sampling 
process- Mathematical modelling of sampling process- Data reconstruction-
Effect of sampling period- Modelling discrete-time systems –Review of Z-
transform-Mapping of s-plane to z-plane- Pulse transfer function-Warping 
effect 
 
9 
2 
Stability analysis of discrete time system:-  Jury stability test, stability 
analysis using bi-linear transformation.  
Time response of discrete systems: Transient and steady state responses, 
time response parameters of a prototype second order system. 
Design of digital control systems--Digital compensator design using 
frequency response plots, 
 
12 

 
 
Digital compensator design using root locus plots, z plane synthesis. 
3 
Discrete state space model- Introduction to state variable model- canonical 
forms-Characteristic equation, state transition matrix-Solution to discrete 
state equation. Stability- Lyapunov stability theorem 
7 
4 
Pole placement and observer design-Controllability and observability-State 
feedback design-Pole placement by state feedback-Set point tracking 
controller-Full order observer-Reduced order observer- Output feedback 
design 
 
8

SEMESTER S7 
CYBER SECURITY FOR INDUSTRIAL AUTOMATION 
 
Course Code 
PEICT742 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
Course Objectives: 
1. Study the importance of cybersecurity in industries. 
 
2. Understanding the architecture and communication protocols used in ICS.  
3. Conducting risk assessments specific to industrial automation systems. 
4. Developing risk mitigation strategies and contingency plans. 
5. Bridging the gap between Information Technology (IT) and Operational Technology (OT) 
security practices 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Overview of industrial automation systems (e.g., SCADA, DCS, PLC). 
Importance of cybersecurity in protecting critical infrastructure. Key 
differences between IT (Information Technology) and OT (Operational 
Technology) networks. 
Fundamentals of Cybersecurity 
Basics of cybersecurity: threats, vulnerabilities, and risks. 
 
8 
2 
 Industrial Control Systems (ICS) Architecture 
Components of ICS: sensors, actuators, controllers, and communication 
protocols Understanding network topologies in industrial environments. 
Typical architectures (e.g., Purdue model). Threat Landscape for Industrial   
cyber threats to ICS (e.g., malware, ransomware, insider threats). 
Case studies of historical cyber incidents in industrial settings. 
 
9 
3 
Cyber attacks 
Impact of cyber-attacks on industrial operations and safety. 
   Security Challenges and Vulnerabilities in ICS, 
Specific vulnerabilities in ICS components and protocols (e.g., Insecure 
10 

 
 
protocols, lack of authentication). 
Human factors: challenges in securing ICS due to operational needs and 
legacy systems. 
 Risk Assessment and Management for ICS Conducting risk assessments 
specific to industrial environments. 
Identifying critical assets and vulnerabilities. 
Developing risk mitigation strategies and incident response 
4 
Secure Design and Configuration of ICS 
Best practices for secure system design and architecture. 
Secure configuration of ICS components (e.g., PLCs, HMIs). 
Principles of secure coding and application development for ICS. 
Network security 
 Network Security for ICS Segmentation and isolation strategies for ICS 
networks. 
Secure communication protocols (e.g., TLS, VPNs) and encryption 
methods. Intrusion detection and prevention systems (IDPS) for ICS. 
encryption methods. 
 Emerging Technologies and Future Trends 
IoT (Internet of Things) and IIoT (Industrial Internet of Things) in 
industrial cybersecurity. 
 
10

SEMESTER S7 
INDUSTRIAL PROCESS CONTROL 
Course Code 
PEICT743 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
Course Objectives: 
1. To provide students with a comprehensive understanding of industrial process control and 
its applications in various industrial sectors. 
2. To familiarise students with instrumentation symbols and standards as per ISA and the 
control of key industrial processes. 
3. To equip students with the skills to analyse, design, and implement control strategies for 
reactors, distillation towers, heat exchangers, pumps, and compressors. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction to Industrial Process Control and Instrumentation 
Standards (8 Hours) 
Introduction to Industrial Process Control. 
Instrumentation Symbols as per ISA Standards: Purpose, scope, 
identification of the systems, function identification, loop identification, 
instrument line symbols, general instrument or function symbols, control 
valve body symbols, actuator symbols, symbols of self-actuated regulators, 
symbols for actuator action, primary element symbols, symbols of heat 
transfer elements, symbols of pump and compressor, symbols of process 
pressure vessels. 
8  
 
2 
Instrumentation and Control of Chemical Reactors and Distillation 
Towers (10 Hours) 
Instrumentation and Control of Chemical Reactors: Flow sheet symbol, 
temperature control, simple temperature control scheme, the valve used in 
the temperature control scheme, the temperature response of an 
uncontrolled chemical reactor to step changes in load, recirculated cooling 
10 

 
 
water configuration, temperature gradient, cascade control, pressure 
control, maximised production by constraint optimisation. 
Instrumentation and Control of Distillation Towers: Distillation 
equipment, column, bubble point and dew point, process of distillation 
tower, flow sheet symbol, column variables, guidelines for identifying the 
manipulating variable, column pressure control, column pressure control 
with liquid distillate and inert, column pressure control with liquid 
distillate and negligible inert, column pressure control with vapour 
distillate and inert, vacuum system, feed control, feed flow rate, variable 
column feed, feed temperature, boil-up control, reflux control. 
3 
Control of Heat Exchangers (9 Hours) 
Different types of heat exchangers, process characteristics, terminology, 
degrees of freedom (DOF), liquid-to-liquid heat exchanger, control of 
liquid-to-liquid heat exchanger using two-way valve, control of liquid-to-
liquid heat exchanger using bypass control, balancing the three-way valve, 
replacing 
three-way valve using two two-way valve, steam heater, steam throttling, 
condensate throttling, level control, bypass 
control in steam heater, cascade loop on steam heater, condenser, control 
of condenser, reboiler, control of reboiler. 
9  
4 
Control of Pumps and Compressors (9 Hours) 
Control of Pumps: System curves, constant static head, friction pressure 
component, control of centrifugal pumps, head capacity curve, operating 
point of pump, on-off level control, on-off flow control, on-off pressure 
control, throttling flow control, control of rotary pump, on-off control, 
throttling and safety control. 
Control of Centrifugal Compressors: Capacity control method used, curves 
of centrifugal compressor, control of centrifugal 
compressor, suction throttling constant pressure system, suction throttling 
mostly friction system, discharge throttling mostly friction system, surge 
control (fixed setpoint), antisurge control. 
9

Course Type 
Theory 
Course Objectives: 
1. Understand the fundamentals of multivariable control systems, including process behavior, 
control aims, feedback, and model considerations. 
2. Develop skills in linear system representation, analysis, and solutions to control problems 
with practical applications such as a simple distillation column.

No.

Systems, Implementation and Structural Issues................................................

SEMESTER S7 
VIRTUAL INSTRUMENTATION 
Course Code 
PEICT745 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
5/3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
Course Objectives: 
1. Develop proficiency in using LabVIEW for graphical system design, virtual instrumentation, 
and modular programming to create, manage, and execute complex engineering processes. 
2. Gain hands-on experience with data acquisition, instrument control, and advanced data 
visualization techniques, integrating hardware and software components effectively for 
comprehensive engineering solutions. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Graphical system design 
Graphical system design (GSD) model-design flow with GSD-virtual 
instrumentation-virtual instrument and traditional instrument-hardware and 
software in virtual instrumentation-virtual instrumentation for test, control 
and design-virtual instrumentation in the engineering process-virtual 
instruments beyond personal computer- graphical system design using 
LabVIEW-graphical programming and textual programming. 
Introduction to LabVIEW 
Advantages of LabVIEW- software environment-creating and saving a vi -
front panel toolbar- block diagram toolbar-palettes -shortcut menus - 
property dialog boxes - front panel controls and indicators- block diagram-
data types -data flow program-LabVIEW documentation resources - 
keyboard shortcuts. 
Modular programming 
Modular programming in LabVIEW - build a vi front panel and block 
diagram-icon and connector pane - creating an icon - building a connector 
pane- displaying subVIs and express vis as icons or expandable nodes - 
creating subVIs from sections of a vi - opening and editing subVIs - 
 
9 

 
 
placing subVIs on block diagrams- saving subVIs - creating a stand-alone 
application. 
2 
Repetition and loops 
For loops - while loops - structure tunnels- terminals inside or outside 
loops - shift registers-feedback nodes- control timing- communicating 
among multiple loops - local variables - global variables. 
Arrays 
Arrays in LabVIEW - creating one-dimensional array controls, indicators 
and constants - creating two-dimensional arrays-creating multidimensional 
arrays- initializing arrays - deleting elements, rows, columns and pages 
within arrays- inserting elements, rows, columns and pages into - replacing 
elements, rows, columns, and pages within arrays- array functions - auto 
indexing - creating two-dimensional arrays using loops - identification of 
data structure (scalar and array) using wires - using auto-indexing to set 
the for loop count - matrix operations with arrays-polymorphism. 
Clusters 
Creating cluster controls and indicators- creating cluster constant - order of 
cluster elements - cluster operations - assembling clusters- disassembling 
clusters - conversion between arrays and clusters - error handling- error 
cluster. 
 
10 
3 
Plotting data 
types of waveforms - waveform graphs-waveform charts-waveform data 
type- XY graphs-intensity graphs and charts-digital waveform graphs-3d 
graphs - customizing graphs and charts-customizing graphs-customizing 3d 
graphs - customizing charts-dynamically formatting waveform graphs -
configuring a graph or chart - displaying special planes on the XY graph. 
Structures 
Case 
structures-sequence 
structures-customizing 
structures- 
timed 
structures- formula nodes - event structure - LabVIEW mathscript. 
Strings and file i/o 
Creating string controls and indicators - string functions-editing, formatting 
and parsing strings - formatting strings - configuring string controls and 
indicators- basics of file input/output - choosing a file I/O format - 
LabVIEW data directory - file i/o VIs - creating a relative path. 
9 
4 
Instrument Control 
Introduction - GPIB communication - hardware specifications - software 
 
8 

 
 
architecture - instrument i/o assistant – visa- instrument - serial port 
communications - data transfer rate - serial port standards - using other 
interfaces. 
Data acquisition 
Transducers - signals- signal conditioning- DAQ hardware configuration - 
DAQ hardware - analog inputs - analog outputs - counters - digital I/O 
(DIO) – DAQ software architecture- DAQ assistant- channels and task 
configuration - selecting and configuring a data acquisition device- 
components of computer based measurement system

Course Objectives: 
1. Explore the history of aviation and space flight, including airplane and space vehicle 
anatomy, aerodynamics, flight performance, and rocket propulsion principles. 
2. Understand the operation and application of various flight and navigation instruments, 
including GPS, GNSS, automatic pilots, and advanced inertial sensors used in guidance and 
avionics systems.

MODERN METHODS OF INSTRUMENT ANALYSIS 
Course Code

(L: T:P: R)

Course Type 
Theory 
Course Objectives: 
1. Gain a solid understanding of the fundamental principles behind modern analytical 
instruments. 
 
2. Learn the theoretical foundations and practical applications of various modern analytical 
techniques used in chemical and biochemical analysis. 
3. Learn how to select appropriate instruments based on analytical needs. 
4. Develop skills in data acquisition, interpretation, and analysis using modern software and 
computational tools. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
 Overview of Instrumental analysis - Review What is analytical science, 
Quantitative and qualitative measurements- Interpretation of analytical 
results, Basic tools available-Concentration and various methods of 
expressing concentration and standard followed during chemical analysis-
Various online and offline sources available-Overview of Food and Drug 
Laws and Regulations-Regulatory affairs, Agencies for implementing 
regulation.Various regulatory protocols, USFDA, ICH Guidelines etc. 
WHO guidelines-The Central Drugs Standard Control Organisation 
(CDSCO- International Organization for Standardization (ISO). 
 
10 
2 
   Thermal Analytical Techniques- Thermogravimetry (TG)-Differential    
Thermal analysis  
(DTA)-Differential Scanning calorimetry (DSC)- Theories of different 
thermal methods, TG, DTA and DSC methods, Instrumentation, Different 
furnaces, Crucibles, Gas handling system, mass flow controllers, crucible 
and ceramic materials used in thermal analysis. Interpretation of data,  
 
9 

 
 
combined techniques like TG-MS. 
3 
Electro analytical methods -(CV, DPV,    LSV)-Common electrochemical 
methods, Cyclic voltametry, systems of reversible, irreversible and quasi 
reversible systems, analysis of redox molecules using CV. 
voltametry analysis basics and application, Application of LSV in hydrogen 
and oxygen evolution reaction.  
9 
4 
Water quality 
Water quality testing parameters, temperature, dissolved oxygen, pH, 
conductivity, ORP, and turbidity. Standard protocols for testing water, 
WHO standards on water quality,  
Water contamination and purification methods 
 
8

SEMESTER S7 
INSTRUMENTATION FOR AGRICULTUTRE 
Course Code 
PEICT753 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
Course Objectives: 
1. To expose the students about various instruments used in agriculture 
2. To teach the design of greenhouses using various instruments 
3. To impart ideas about modern technologies used in agriculture  
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
  Soil Science & Sensors 
Soil science :  fundamental definitions & relationships 
properties of soil :  index properties of soil,  Engineering properties 
of soil,  physical properties of soil 
permeability & seepage analysis,  Mohr’s circle of stress 
Necessity of instrumentation & control for agriculture 
Sensors and transducers: definitions,  introduction to sonic 
anemometers,  hygrometers,  thermocouples,  close path gas 
analysers,  introduction to various biosensors 
 
9 
2 
  Instrumentation in industrial Continuous & Batch processes 
Idea about continuous and batch processes 
Flow diagram of sugar plant, sensors & instrumentation set up 
Flow diagram of fermenter, sensors & instrumentation set up 
Flow diagram of dairy industry & instrumentation set up for it 
Juice extraction control process & instrumentation set up.  
Oil extraction plant and instrumentation set up for it. 
Pesticides manufacturing process and control 
 
9 

 
 
3 
  Instrumentation in Irrigation 
Necessity of irrigation in agriculture 
Evapotranspiration and its measurement methods 
irrigation methods: overhead, centre pivot, lateral move, micro 
irrigation systems & the comparison of different irrigation systems 
soil moisture measurement methods: resistance-based method, 
voltage based method, thermal based method 
Water distribution & management control, Auto drip & sprinkler 
irrigation systems,  
Irrigation canal management systems 
upstream & downstream control concept 
Introduction to SCADA , Applications of SCADA in agriculture 
11 
4 
Greenhouse Parameters & Instrumentation 
Greenhouse effect, Concept & construction of green houses, 
ventilation, cooling & heating, wind speed, temperature & 
humidity, soil moisture, rain gauge, carbon dioxide enrichment 
measurement & control 
implementation of hydraulic, pneumatic & electronics control 
circuits in harvesters cotton pickers, tractor 
Classification of pumps: pump characteristics, pump selection & 
installation. 
 
9

SEMESTER S7 
INDUSTRIAL DRIVES AND CONTROL 
Course Code 
PEICT754 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
Course Objectives: 
1. Understand the fundamental concepts of electric drives, including types, factors influencing 
selection, thermal characteristics, and load variations for optimal power rating selection. 
2. Gain knowledge of mechanical and speed-torque characteristics of different motors, braking 
methods, starting techniques, and advanced speed control methods for DC and AC drives, 
with practical applications. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction: Basic elements-types of electric drives-factors influencing 
electric drives-heating and cooling curves loading conditions and classes of 
duty-Selection of power rating for drive motors with regard to thermal 
overloading and load variation factors 
 
9 
2 
Drive motor characteristics: Mechanical characteristics- speed- torque 
characteristics of various types of load and drive motors - braking of 
electrical motors-dc motors: shunt, series, compound motors-single phase 
and three phase induction motors 
 
9 
3 
Starting methods: Types of d.c motor starters-typical control circuits for 
shunt and series motors-three phase squirrel and slip ring induction motors 
9 
4 
Conventional and solid-state speed control of D.C and A.C Drives 
Speed: control of DC series and shunt motors-Armature and field control, 
ward-Leonard control system using controlled rectifiers and DC choppers –
applications 
Speed control 
of three phase induction motor-Voltage control, 
voltage/frequency control, slip power recovery scheme-using inverters and 
AC voltage regulators-applications 
 
9
