SEMESTER S7 
NON LINEAR DYNAMICS AND CHAOS 
Course Code 
PEICT756 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
Course Objectives: 
1. Understand the fundamental concepts of nonlinear dynamics and chaos. 
2.  Analyze dynamical systems using phase plane techniques. 
3. Explore the behavior of systems near bifurcation points. 
4. Investigate the routes to chaos and the characteristics of chaotic systems 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Overview of Dynamical Systems-Chaos, Fractals and Dynamics – History 
of Dynamics – Nonlinear systems. 
One-Dimensional Flows: Fixed Points and Stability-Linear Stability 
Analysis-Existence and Uniqueness – Potentials. 
 
9 
2 
Bifurcations 
Saddle-Node Bifurcation-Transcritical and Pitchfork Bifurcations Imperfect 
Bifurcations and Applications 
Flows on the Circle 
Introduction to Circle Maps -Phase-Locked Solutions-Bifurcations and 
Chaos in Circle Maps 
 
9 
3 
Two-Dimensional Flows 
 Phase Plane Analysis-Linear Systems and Phase Portraits-Nonlinear 
Systems and Limit Cycles-Limit Cycles and Oscillators-Van der Pol 
9 

 
 
Oscillator-Relaxation Oscillations-Perturbation Methods 
Bifurcations  
Hopf Bifurcation-Global Bifurcations and Homoclinic Orbits 
 Bifurcation Diagrams and Routes to Chaos 
4 
Chaos 
Lorenz Equations and Strange Attractors-Lyapunov Exponents-Fractals and 
Dimension 
One Dimensional Maps Introduction –Fixed points and Cobwebs - Logistic 
Map: Numerics- Logistic Map: Analysis – Periodic windows – Liapunov 
Exponents. 
 
9

Course Outcomes (COs) 
At the end of the course students should be able to:  
Course Outcome 
Bloom’s 
Knowledge 
Level (KL) 
CO1 
explain the concepts of fixed points and stability in one-dimensional 
flows, including performing linear stability analysis and understanding 
the implications of existence and uniqueness theorems in nonlinear 
systems. 
K2 
CO2 
demonstrate an understanding of various types of bifurcations, such as 
saddle-node, transcritical, and pitchfork bifurcations, including 
recognizing imperfect bifurcations and their applications in different 
dynamical systems. 
K2 
CO3 
describe and analyse phase plane dynamics in two-dimensional 
systems, including constructing and interpreting phase portraits for 
both linear and nonlinear systems, and understanding the behavior of 
limit cycles and oscillators. 
K3 
CO4 
understand   chaotic systems, including the Lorenz equations, strange 
attractors, and Lyapunov exponents and the concept of fractals and 
dimensions, and analyze the behavior of one-dimensional maps, such 
as the logistic map, using techniques like cobwebbing and identifying 
periodic windows and Lyapunov exponents. 
K2 
Note: K1- Remember, K2- Understand, K3- Apply, K4- Analyse, K5- Evaluate, K6- Create

SEMESTER S7 
SYSTEM IDENTIFICATION AND ADAPTIVE 
CONTROL 
Course Code 
PEICT757 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
PCICT403, 
PCICT501, 
PBICT604
Course Type 
Theory 
Course Objectives: 
1. To introduce various model structures for system identification 
2. To impart knowledge on parametric and non-parametric identification 
3. To introduce the concept of adaptation techniques and control 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
System Identification 
Models for identification: Models of LTI systems: Linear Models-State 
space Models-OE model- Model sets, Structures and identifiability-Models 
for Time-varying and Non-linear systems: Models with Nonlinearities – 
Non-linear state-space models-Black box models, Fuzzy models 
9 
2 
Non-parametric and parametric identification: Transient response and 
Correlation Analysis – Frequency response analysis – Spectral Analysis – 
Least Square – Recursive Least Square –Forgetting factor- Maximum 
Likelihood – Instrumental Variable methods 
9 
3 
Introduction to adaptive control 
Linear feedback; effects of process variations; adaptive schemes; 
Introduction to deterministic self-tuning regulators; pole placement design; 
indirect self-tuning regulator; design of minimum variance and moving 
average controllers; adaptive predictive control 
9 
4 
Model Reference Adaptive Systems 
Introduction to model-reference adaptive systems; Lyapunov theory; design 
 
9 

 
 
of MRAS using Lyapunov theory; Bounded-input bounded-output stability; 
applications to adaptive control.

SEMESTER 7 
IOT AND APPLICATIONS 
Course Code 
PEICT755 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:1 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
4 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any)

Course Objectives: 
1. 
Gain a comprehensive understanding of IoT technology, including its definitions, architecture, 
functional blocks, communication models, enabling technologies, and deployment templates. 
2. 
Learn about IoT and M2M differences, sensor networks, communication protocols, IoT 
privacy and security solutions, and practical applications such as smart city IoT architecture 
and Raspberry Pi interfacing and programming. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction to IoT technology: Definitions and Characteristics of IoT, IoT 
Architectural View, Physical Design of IOT, Logical Design of IoT- IoT

9 
2 
IoT and M2M- M2M, Difference between IoT and M2M, SDN and NFV

9 
3 
Unified Data Standards –Protocols –IEEE 802.15.4 -The Physical Layer,

802.15.4: 802.15.4e and 802.15.4g–Modbus– ZigBee-Zigbee Architecture- 
LoRaWAN -Standardization and Alliances, Physical Layer, MAC Layer, 
Topology, LTE-M, NB-IoT-Network layer –The next generation: IP-based 
protocols 
9 
4 
Raspberry-Pi-Raspberry-Pi Interfaces (serial, SPI, I2C). Raspberry Pi 
interfacing and programming examples using python (LED, switch, sensor, 
 
9 

 
 
serial, SPI, I2C devices). IoT privacy, security and vulnerabilities solutions, 
vulnerabilities, security requirements, threat analysis, security tomography, 
layered attacker model, Identity management, access control, secure 
message communication. Smart City IoT Architecture-Street Layer, City 
Layer, Data Center Layer, Services Layer.

SEMESTER S7 
AUTOMOBILE INSTRUMENTATION 
Course Code 
OEICT721 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0

60 
Credits

2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
Course Objectives: 
1. To make them understand fundamentals of 4 stroke engine 
2. To expose the students to the concepts of various sensors used in automobile systems. 
3. To teach the basic and advanced controls in automotive systems 
4. To impart ideas on hybrid and electric vehicles, ADAS, GPS 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
 Fundamentals of Vehicles  
Engine basic concepts (4 strokes), Starting & charging system, 
onboard diagnostic system, Vehicle motion control, Digital cruise 
control, and current trends in modern automobiles. 
 
9 
2 
Engine management systems  
Basic sensor arrangement and types of sensors: oxygen sensors, crank 
angle position sensors, vehicle speed sensors, flow sensors, 
temperature, air mass flow sensors, throttle position sensors, 
electronic ignition, and EGR for exhaust emission control. 
 
9 
3 
 Automobile Chassis Electronic Control System 
 
Principles of electronic braking, automatic transmission electronic 
control circuit, cruise control circuit, electronic steering control theory, 
ABS, ASR, ESP, and other electronic control methods. 
auto Body Electronic Control Technology, Automotive central 
locking, and anti-theft system control technology. Air bag technology 
 
9 

 
 
4 
Latest  Automotive Instrumentation 
 
Concepts of hybrid technology and its classification. Introduction to 
electric vehicles and classifications. Introduction to ADAS (Automatic 
Driver Assist Systems). GPS Navigation and GPS System Structure. 
 
9

SEMESTER S7 
MEASURMENTS AND TRANSDUCERS 
Course Code 
OEICT722 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
OEICT 611 
Course Type 
Theory 
Course Objectives: 
1. Learn various transducer types and their principles. Differentiate between primary and 
secondary transducers. 
2. Understand principles and functions of electrical measuring instruments, current and 
potential transformers and resistance measurement techniques with bridges and 
ohmmeters. 
3. Master techniques for measuring force, acceleration, torque, power, and fluid properties. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Transducers 
Definition of transducers - primary and secondary transducers. 
Principles of variable resistance transducers – Potentiometers - Strain 
gauges 
Piezo electric transducers, materials and properties, modes of deformation, 
Hall effect transducers.                                      
Principle, type and construction of variable inductive transducers, Different 
types of self and mutual inductance transducers, LVDT and RVDT. Uses, 
advantages and disadvantages of inductive transducers.                              
Principle, types and construction of different types of variable capacitance 
transducers. Uses, advantages and disadvantages of capacitive transducers, 
LDR.                                                 
 
9 
2 
Electrical Measuring Instruments 
Indicating Instruments: Principle, types of control and damping; Moving 
coil Instruments: Types (permanent magnet, dynamometer type meters); 
 
9 

 
 
Moving Iron Instruments: Attraction and repulsion type, Principles and 
torque equation; Wattmeters: Dynamometer type wattmeter, Principles and 
torque equation; Measurement of single phase and three phase 
  power; true RMS meter; Errors and Compensation. 
3 
Transformers 
Current transformers and Potential transformers; use of instrument 
transformers with wattmeter. 
Bridges and Potentiometers 
Measurement of resistance: Ohmmeter, Megger, Wheatstone bridge; 
Kelvin’s double bridge; Phasor diagram; AC bridges: Measurements of 
inductance using Maxwell and Anderson bridges; Measurements of 
capacitance using Schering Bridge; Potentiometer: General principle; 
Modern form of dc potentiometers; Vernier dial principle; Standardization. 
9 
4 
Force Measurement - Platform balance - Force to displacement 
conversion - Proving ring - Conversion of force to hydraulic pressure - 
Piezoelectric force transducer. 
Measurement of acceleration  
Preliminary ideas - Characteristics of a spring - mass - damper system - 
Piezoelectric accelerometer - Laser Doppler Vibrometer - Fiber Optic 
Accelerometer 
Measurement of torque and power - Mechanical brake arrangement - 
Prony brake - Electric generator as a dynamometer - Measure shear stress 
on the shaft - Tachometer - Mechanical Device - Non-contact optical RPM 
meter. 
Fluid properties: Density, surface tension, capillarity and viscosity; 
Newton’s law of viscosity; Fluid Statics; Pascal’s law, Centre of pressure, 
Buoyancy, Metacentre; Basic equations of fluid flow; continuity, 
momentum and energy equations; Bernoulli’s equations 
 
9

SEMESTER S7 
BIOMEDICAL INSTRUMENTATION 
Course Code 
OEICT723 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0

60

2 Hrs. 30 Min.

None 
 
Course Type 
Theory 
Course Objectives: 
1. Gain fundamental knowledge of biopotential acquisition and analysis:  
2. Develop an understanding of signal conditioning principles for biomedical 
applications 
3. Become familiar with the measurement of various physiological parameters  
                                                            SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
BASIC ANATOMY AND PHYSIOLOGY: Origin of bio potential and its 
propagation, Nervous system, Muscular system, Cardiovascular system, 
Respiratory System. 
BIOPOTENTIAL 
ELECTRODES: 
Electrode-electrolyte 
interface, 
electrode–skin interface, half-cell potential, Contact impedance, polarization 
effects of electrode – non polarizable electrodes. Types of electrodes - 
surface, needle and micro electrodes and their equivalent circuits. Recording 
problems - motion artifacts- Monopolar and  bipolar electrode configurations  
 
9 
2 
Bio signals characteristics – frequency and amplitude ranges. ECG – 
Einthoven ‘s triangle, standard 12 lead system, Principles of vector 
cardiography. EEG – 10-20 electrode system, unipolar, bipolar and average 
mode. EMG– unipolar and bipolar mode. 
SIGNAL CONDITIONING CIRCUITS:  
Need for bio-amplifier - differential bio-amplifier, Design of bio-amplifiers 
for the measurement of physiological variables. Power line interference, 
Band pass filtering. 
 
9 

 
 
Working of isolation amplifiers, (transformer, capacitive and optical 
isolation), isolated DC amplifier and AC carrier amplifier. (Circuit diagram 
and working only) 
3 
MEASUREMENT OF NON-ELECTRICAL PARAMETERS: 
Temperature and pulse rate measurements. Blood Pressure: indirect methods 
- Auscultatory method, oscillometric method, direct methods: electronic 
manometer, Pressure amplifiers, Systolic, diastolic, mean detector circuit. 
Blood flow and cardiac output measurement: Indicator dilution, thermal 
dilution and dye dilution method, Electromagnetic and ultrasound blood flow 
measurement. 
Pulmonary 
function 
measurements-Spirometer, 
Photo 
plethysmography, Body plethysmography.  
7 
4 
ELECTRICAL SAFETY IN MEDICAL ENVIRONMENT: 
Types of Electrical hazards, Physiological effects of electric current –  
Threshold Values for Electrical Shock, shock hazards from electrical 
equipment – leakage current-Instruments for checking safety parameters of 
biomedical equipment, Methods of accident prevention, Electrical Safety 
Standards 
ASSISTIVE AND THERAPEUTIC EQUIPMENTS: 
Pacemakers, defibrillators, ventilators, diathermy, Heart-Lung machine and 
dialyzers. (Diagrams and Basic working only) 
BIOMEDICAL IMAGING  
X-ray, Computed Tomography, Ultrasound, Magnetic resonance Imaging. 
(Diagrams and Basic working only) 
 
11

SEMESTER S8 
OPTOELECTRONICS AND INSTRUMENTATION 
Course Code 
PEICT861 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
Course Objectives: 
1. To understand the principles of interferometers, Lasers and its applications 
 
2. To gain knowledge about fiber optics in instrumentation and its applications 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Interferometers: Fabry-Perot and Michelson interferometers – Interference 
filters – Interferometric method of measurement of optical components – 
Optical spectrum analyser. 
Raman Spectroscopy, Raman effect. 
 
7 
2 
Modulation of light: Birefringence – Optical activity – Electro-optic effect 
– Magneto-optic devices – Acousto-optic effect. Display devices: 
Electroluminescence – Injection Luminescence – Light emitting diode – 
Plasma displays – Liquid crystal displays. Opto-couplers ,Optrodes 
 
9 
3 
Lasers: Principles of operation –Einstein relations – population inversion– 
Classes of lasers – Solid state: Nd-YAG laser, Ruby laser, gas: He-Ne laser, 
Argon ion laser, CO2 laser and liquid dye lasers – Q-switching and mode 
locking ,cavity dumping Application of LASER - Distance, length, 
velocity, acceleration, current and voltage measurements. Material 
processing: Laser heating, melting, scribing, splicing, welding and 
trimming of materials, removal and vaporization, calculation of power 
requirements. Laser gyroscope. 
Holography – Principles and applications – Pollution monitoring, industry 
and biomedical applications 
9 
4 
Optical fibers: Introduction to optical fiber – Fiber characteristics, Light 
guidance through fibers – Different types of fibers– Losses in the optical 
 
11 

 
 
fiber – Dispersion – optical time domain reflectometer-Advantages and 
disadvantages of optical fibers, Connectors and splices 
 Applications of optical fibres: optical fibre communication- Selection of 
optical fibers – fibre optic sensors – measurement of temperature, pressure, 
displacement, strain, acceleration and fluid level

Course Code

Course Type 
Theory 
Course Objectives: 
1. Gain a comprehensive understanding of safety hazards, risks, and the principles of Safety 
Instrumented Systems (SIS), including their design, implementation, and standards 
compliance (IEC 61508, IEC 61511, ISA 84.01-2003). 
2. Develop the ability to identify, assess, and mitigate occupational safety and health hazards, 
utilizing accident theories and models to prevent incidents and ensure a safe working 
environment.

SEMESTER S8 
INSTRUMENTATION AND CONTROL IN LARGE SCALE 
INDUSTRIES 
Course Code 
PEICT864 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
PEICT 743, 
PCICT205 
Course Type 
Theory 
Course Objectives: 
1. Gain knowledge of various chemical and biological treatment processes, including oxidation, 
reduction, and neutralization, and their control mechanisms. 
2. Learn the control systems and optimization techniques for evaporators, clean rooms, steam 
boilers, and oil industry instrumentation, focusing on maintaining efficiency, safety, and 
environmental compliance. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Instrumentation and Control of Effluent Water and Waste Water 
Treatment 
Basics, chemical oxidation, cyanide destruction process, batch oxidation, 
continuous oxidation, chlorinator, chemical reduction, reduction of 
hexavalent chromium, dichlorination, neutralisation, valve rangeability 
required, precise neutralisation, single reagent control, feedforward 
feedback neutralisation control, precipitation, lime softening, biological 
control, chlorination-based disinfection control 
9 
2 
Control of Evaporator 
Evaporator terminology, single effect evaporator, multiple effect 
evaporator, economy, capacity, modelling, steady-state model, control 
systems for evaporators, feedback control, cascade control, feedforward 
control: process dynamics, process dynamics with feedback trim, steam 
enthalpy, absolute pressure. 
9 
3 
Control and Optimisation of Clean Room 
Need of cleanroom, clean-room, subzone optimisation, pressure control, 
9 

 
 
elimination of draft, temperature control, humidity control, flow control, 
optimisation of zones, envelope optimisation, plantwide optimisation, 
material balance control, heat balance control, mechanical design 
limitations, humidity control, exhaust air control. 
4 
Control of Steam Boiler 
Flow sheet symbol, process of boiler, safety interlocks, basic boiler 
controls, load sharing control, boiler control with alternative pressure or 
flow master, feedforward control with feedback trim, fuel controls, air flow 
control, damper and fan controls, furnace draft control, fuel-air ratio, 
proportional compensation in air-fuel ratio control. 
Instrumentation and Control used in Oil Industry 
separators, test separators and well test, first stage separator, second stage 
separator, third stage or final stage separator, coalescer, electrostatic, gas 
treatment, heat exchanger, HVAC. 
 
9

SEMESTER S8 
CORROSION CONTROL 
Course Code 
PEICT866 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
Course Objectives: 
1. It aims to explain the concept of corrosion and different types of corrosion, and also helps the 
students to select a suitable corrosion control or prevention technique. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction to Corrosion 
Historical background, definitions, corrosive environment, consequences of 
corrosion, cost of corrosion, breakdown of spending on corrosion, corrosion 
science and corrosion engineering, functional aspects of corrosion. 
Basic Concepts in Corrosion 
 
Anodic and cathodic reaction, Anodic reactions characteristics, Cathodic 
reactions characteristics, types of corrosion cells, mechanism of corrosion of 
Iron, concept of free energy, reversible electrode potential, concentration 
cell, liquid junction potential, application of free energy to corrosion cells, 
Nernst equation, sign convention, reference electrodes 
 
9 
2 
Corrosion Kinetics and Measurement 
Faraday’s Laws, Corrosion Kinetics, Helmholtz double layer, reverse 
reaction (cathodic reaction), departure from equilibrium, measurement of 
corrosion, determination of corrosion rates by electrochemical 
measurements, polarisation linearization, kinetics of passivity, definition of 
important electrochemical parameters for active passive metals, control of 
passivity, effect of environment. 
 
9 

 
 
3 
Cathodic Protection 
Basis of cathodic protection, working of cathodic protection system, factors 
leading to corrosion of underground metallic structures, electrical basis of 
cathodic protection, electrochemical theory of cathodic protection, anodic 
polarisation, cathodic protection system, components of Galvanic systems, 
impressed current system, protection of submarine pipelines, design 
parameters in cathode protection, measurements in cathodic protection. 
9 
4 
Corrosion Control by Inhibition 
Scope of inhibitor, examples of application of inhibitors, important 
consideration in selection of inhibitors, important terms related to inhibitors, 
classification of inhibitors, description of inhibitors, inorganic anodic 
inhibitors, organic inhibitors, synergistic inhibitors, scaven gers, neutralisers, 
scale inhibitors, rebar inhibitors, inhibitor application techniques, inhibitor 
efficiency and inhibitor concentration 
 
9

SEMESTER S8 
IMAGE PROCESSING 
Course Code 
PEICT865 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
5/3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
PEICT 415 
Course Type 
THEORY 
Course Objectives: 
1. This course will strengthen fundamental knowledge about image processing techniques.  
2. Digital image processing is used in almost all engineering fields and wide range of 
applications in industrial automation, medical, agriculture, security, entertainment, education 
and many more. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Image Fundamentals: Image representation, basic relationship between 
pixels, elements of DIP system, elements ofvisual perception-simple image 
formation model. 
Brightness, contrast, hue, saturation, mach band effect. 
Colour image fundamentals RGB, CMY, HIS models. 
2D Image transforms DFT, its properties, Walsh transform, Hadamard 
transform, Haar transform.DCT and KL transform. 
9 
2 
Image Enhancement 
Spatial domain methods: point processing- intensity transformations, 
histogram processing,image subtraction, image averaging.Spatial filtering- 
smoothing filters, sharpening filters.Frequency domain methods: low pass 
filtering, high pass filtering, homomorphic filter. 
9 
3 
Image Restoration 
 Unconstraint restoration- Lagrange multiplier and constraint restoration. 
Inverse filtering- removal of blur caused by uniform linear motion, Weiner 
filtering, 
Image segmentation 
Classification of Image segmentation techniques, region approach, 
9 

 
 
clustering techniques. 
Classification of edges, edge detection, Hough transform. 
4 
Image Compression 
Need for compression, redundancy, classification of image compression 
schemes, Huffman 
coding, arithmetic coding, dictionary-based compression, transform based 
compression, 
Image compression standards- JPEG& MPEG. 
9

SEMESTER S8 
INDUSTRIAL AUTOMATION 
Course Code 
OEICT831 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
Course Objectives: 
1. Provide an overview of automation concepts, including historical evolution, principles, and 
the importance of automation in modern industries. 
 
2. Introduce students to Programmable Logic Controllers (PLCs) 
3. Explain Supervisory Control and Data Acquisition (SCADA) systems. 
4. Discuss networking fundamentals relevant to industrial automation. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Automation introduction 
Control Systems and Automation Strategy, Evolution of instrumentation 
and control, Role of automation in industries, Benefits of automation, 
Introduction to Descriptive automation tools PLC, DCS, SCADA, Hybrid 
DCS/PLC, Automation strategy evolution, Control system audit, and 
performance criteria. 
 
8 
2 
Instrumentation Standard Protocols 
Definition of protocol, Introduction to Open System Interconnection (OSI) 
model, Communication standard (RS232, RS485), Modbus (ASCII/RTU), 
Introduction to third party interface, concept of OPC (Object linking and 
embedding for Process Control), HART Protocol: Introduction, frame 
structure, programming, implementation examples, benefits, advantages 
and limitation. 
Foundation Fieldbus H1: Introduction, frame structure, programming, 
implementation examples,benefits, advantages and limitation. Comparison 
of HART, Foundation Fieldbus, Device net,Profibus, Controlnet, 
Industrial Ethernet 
 
11 
3 
Programmable logic controllers (PLC) 
9 

 
 
Introduction, architecture, definition of discrete state process control, PLC  
Vs PC, PLC Vs DCS, relay diagram, ladder diagram, ladder diagram 
examples, relay sequencers, timers/counters, high speed counter, PTO, 
PWM  and PID blocks in PLC, PLC design, study of at least one industrial 
PLC. 
4 
Networking fundamentals 
Advance Applications of PLC and SCADA, PLC programming methods as 
per IEC 61131, PLC applications for batch process using SFC, Analog 
Control using PLC, PLC interface to SCADA/DCS using communication 
links (RS232, RS485) and protocols (Modbus ASCII/RTU) 
Distributed Control Systems 
DCS introduction, functions, advantages and limitations, DCS as an 
automation tool to support Enterprise Resources Planning, DCS 
Architecture of different makes, Latest trends and developments. 
 
10

SEMESTER S8 
ENVIRONMENTAL INSTRUMENTATION 
Course Code 
OEICT832 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
Course Objectives: 
1. The aim of environmental instrumentation program is to offer students a basic knowledge of 
Environmental Instrumentation. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction to Environmental Engineering 
An overview of environmental laws and regulations. Necessity of 
Instrumentation & Control for environment, sensor requirement for 
environment, Classification of pollution: Air pollution, water pollution, soil 
pollution, marine pollution, noise pollution, thermal pollution, nuclear 
hazards and hazardous waste, occupational safety and health. Causes, 
Effects and control of all types of Pollution. 
 
9 
2 
Quality of water 
Standards of raw & treated water, sources of water & their natural quality, 
effects of water quality. Water quality parameters: Thermal conductivity, 
dissolved oxygen, anions, turbidity. Water Quality detectors, Opacity 
monitors, conductivity analysers & their application. Spectrometric 
methods- emission spectrograph- atomic absorption spectra. 
 
9 
3 
Air monitoring 
Measurement of ambient air quality. Air pollution control of stationary 
sources: gaseous pollutants and particulate pollutants. Air pollution control 
of mobile sources: automobile emissions. Noise pollution: effect of noise 
pollution on people and community, noise area classification and hearing 
conservation. Noise sources and criteria, noise level measurement, noise 
absorption techniques and noise control. 
9 

 
 
4 
Pollution control in industries 
pollution control in petroleum refineries, fertilizer industries, pulp and 
paper industries, cement industries. Pollution case studies - disaster 
management: floods, earthquake, cyclone and landslides, Environmental 
disaster monitoring. 
Handling and management of hospital wastes. 
 
9

 SEMESTER: S8 
INDUSTRIAL INSTRUMENTATION  
 
Course Code 
OEICT833 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
 
3:0:0:0 
 
ESE Marks 
 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
 
Course Type 
 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
 
1. 
To familiarize the students about various types of temperature, pressure, level, pH, density, 
viscosity, turbidity and conductivity measurement systems 
 
SYLLABUS 
 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
 
 
 
 
 
 
1 
Temperature Measurement 
Definitions and units- Standards of temperature – Thermometry and 
pyrometry- Thermocouples- Peltier effect- Thomson effect- Seebeck 
effect- 
Types 
of 
thermocouples 
(Chromel- 
copper. 
Chromel- 
alumel.copper-constantan, iron-constantan, platinum-rhodium- platinum) 
Cold junction compensation-Signal conditioning for thermocouple-
Thermowells-– Thermopiles- Resistance thermometers- Principle of 
operation- Platinum RTD- Construction of RTDs 
Thermistors, principle and sensor types, manufacturing techniques, 
measuring circuits. Thermometers- Expansion thermometers- Bimetallic 
thermometers – Liquid filled -thermometers- Gas filled thermometers.  
Pyrometry- Stefan Boltzmann’s law- Black body radiation- Total radiation 
pyrometersOptical radiation pyrometers. 
10  
 
 
 
 
2 
Pressure measurement 
Units of pressure – Manometers: Different types, Elastic type pressure 
gauges: Bourdon tube, Bellows, Diaphragms and Capsules – Electrical 
methods: Elastic elements with LVDT and strain gauges – Capacitive 
type pressure gauge – Piezo resistive pressure sensor-Resonator 
pressure sensor –  
High-Pressure sensors: Dead-Weight piston gauge, Bulk modulus 
cellsMeasurement of vacuum: McLeod gauge, Thermal conductivity 
gauge, lionization gauges, Cold cathode type and hot cathode type – 
Pressure gauge selection
8  

 
 
 
 
 
 
3 
Measurement of viscosity  
Definitions, 
units, 
Newtonian 
and 
Non-Newtonian 
behaviour, 
measurement of viscosity using laboratory viscometers, industrial 
viscometers, Viscometer selection and application. 
Measurement of density 
Definitions, units, liquid density measurement, gas densitometers, its 
application and selection. 
Level measurement  
Level measurement: introduction, float level devices, displacer level 
devices, rotating paddle switches, diaphragm and differential pressure 
detectors, 
resistance, 
capacitance and 
RF 
probes, 
radiation, 
conductivity, field effect, thermal, ultrasonic, microwave level 
switches, radar and vibrating type level sensors. Level sensor selection 
and application
10  
 
 
 
 
 
4 
Flow measurement  
Introduction, definitions and units, classification of flow meters, pitot 
tubes, positive displacement liquid meters, positive displacement gas 
flow meters, variable area flow meters. Anemometers: Hot wire/hot 
film anemometer, laser Doppler anemometer (LDA) Electromagnetic 
flow meter, turbine and other rotary element flow meters, ultrasonic 
flow meters, doppler flow meters, cross correlation flow meters, 
vortex flow meters 
 
8
